، فهو أخذه لبعض طرق المتكلمين . أو بمعنى أدق كانت هذه الطرق مشتركة بين المتكلمين والأصوليين كما يذكر إمام الحرمين والزركشي والايجي(٣) . بل ويقرر الايجي أن أدلة العقول الأولى أمس بالفقه منها بالكلام . كما أن مبحث الحد الأصولي ينسب الى علماء أصول الفقه أكثر من نسبته إلى المتكلمين . ولم يكن هذا التأثر من جهة واحدة ، بل كان متبادلاً . فإذا كان علماء أصول الفقه قد أخذوا من المتكلمين بعض الطرق ، فقد أخذ المتكلمون من الأصوليين طرقاً كثيرة . وفي إيجاز نستطيع أن نقرر أنه لا توجد طرق منفصلة لإحدى هاتين الفرقتين بل استخدمت كل منهما نفس الطرق التي استخدمتها الأخرى . وصل المنهج بعد ذلك إلى المدرسة الحنفية . وقد أقام الأحناف الأصول على الفروع ولم يقيموا الفروع على الأصول . فكان بجانب كل فرع أصله الفقهي الذي خرج عنه . أما إقامة الفروع على الأصول فهي المحاولة التي قام بها الشافعي . وصل المنهج إذن إلى الشافعي وكان قد مر عليه تطورات عدة كما رأينا بلغت به حداً كبيراً من النضوج . ولا ينقص من قدر العمل الذي قام به الشافعي . وصول جوهر المنهج القياسي إليه . فقد قام الشافعي بتحليل هذا المنهج وعرضه في صورة منظمة ، وأضاف إليه أبحاثاً كثيرة أهمها المباحث البيانية التي لم يكن الصدر الأول في حاجة إليها ، حين كان الكلام ملكة للعرب . وتوسع في جميع المباحث الأصولية التي عرفت من قبل وأكمل بعضها . وأقام فروع المذهب على الأصول . فالشافعي له في وضع المنهج فضل لا ينكر. يقول الرازي : «كان الناس قبل الشافعي يتكلمون في مسائل أصول الفقه ويستدلون ويعترضون . ولكن ما كان لهم قانون كلي مرجوع اليه في معرفة دلائل الشريعة وفي كيفية معارضتها وترجيحها ـ فاستنبط الشافعي علم أصول الفقه ، ووضع للخلق قانوناً كلياً يرجع في معرفة مراتب أدلة الشرع اليه »(١) . ويقول مصطفى عبد الرازق : « كان اتجاه المذاهب الفقهية قبل الشافعي الى جمع المسائل وترتيبها وردها إلى أدلتها التفصيلية خصوصاً عندما تكون دلائلها نصوصاً وأهل الحديث لكثرة اعتمادهم على النص كانوا أكثر تعرضاً لذكر الدلائل من أهل الرأي . فلما جاء الشافعي بمذهبه الجديد كان قد درس المذهبين . ولاحظ ما فيهما من نقص بدا له أن يكمله . وأخذ ينقض بعض التعريفات من ناحية خروجها عن متابعة نظام متحد في طريقة الاستنباط »(٢) وهذه الطريقة طريقة فلسفية بحتة .
Until it becomes probable that the judgment of God Almighty regarding them is one. And that became a legal proof by consensus of them. And it is qiyas(1). Moreover, they arrived at the topic of preferences (tarjihat) especially in the domain of reports (akhbar). The usuli methodology did not remain static, but rather it grew and new methods were added to it at the hands of the school of qiyas in general, and in Iraq in particular. And it is completely wrong to say that this development itself occurred under foreign influences, the most important of which is Aristotelian logic. It had been translated into Arabic and spread in various circles, in addition to the fact that many of the jurists of Iraq were non-Arabs, and Aristotelian logic had been translated from a distant era into Persian(2). As for what the usuli methodology submitted to, it is its adoption of some methods of the mutakallimun. Or more precisely, these methods were shared between the mutakallimun and the usuliyyun, as mentioned by Imam al-Haramayn, al-Zarkashi, and al-Iji(3). Rather, al-Iji affirms that the proofs of the primary intellects are more connected to fiqh than to kalam. Likewise, the topic of the usuli definition (al-hadd al-usuli) is attributed to the scholars of usul al-fiqh more than its attribution to the mutakallimun. And this influence was not one-sided, but mutual. So if the scholars of usul al-fiqh took some methods from the mutakallimun, the mutakallimun took many methods from the usuliyyun. In summary, we can affirm that there are no separate methods for either of these two groups; rather, each used the same methods that the other used. The methodology then reached the Hanafi school. The Hanafis established the usul on the furu' and did not establish the furu' on the usul. So alongside each branch was its juristic origin from which it issued. As for establishing the furu' on the usul, that is the attempt made by al-Shafi'i. The methodology then reached al-Shafi'i, having passed through several developments as we saw, reaching a great degree of maturity. And this does not diminish the value of the work that al-Shafi'i did, that the essence of the qiyas methodology reached him. For al-Shafi'i analyzed this methodology and presented it in an organized form, and added to it many investigations, the most important of which are the rhetorical investigations (al-mabahith al-bayaniyya) which the early generation had no need for, when speech (al-kalam) was an innate faculty for the Arabs. He expanded on all the usuli investigations that were known before and completed some of them. And he established the branches of the madhhab on the usul. So al-Shafi'i has an undeniable merit in establishing the methodology. Al-Razi says: 'People before al-Shafi'i used to speak about issues of usul al-fiqh, argue, and object. But they had no universal law to refer to in knowing the evidences of the Sharia and how to oppose and prefer them. So al-Shafi'i derived the science of usul al-fiqh, and laid down for the people a universal law to refer to in knowing the ranks of the legal evidences'(1). And Mustafa 'Abd al-Raziq says: 'The direction of the juristic schools before al-Shafi'i was towards collecting issues and arranging them and referring them to their detailed evidences, especially when their evidences were texts, and the people of hadith, due to their heavy reliance on text, were more exposed to mentioning evidences than the people of opinion. When al-Shafi'i came with his new madhhab, he had studied both schools. He noticed the deficiency in both that seemed to him to complete. And he began to refute some definitions from the aspect of their deviating from following a unified system in the method of deduction'(2). And this method is a purely philosophical method.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of the development of usul al-fiqh methodology. It begins by noting that qiyas (analogical reasoning) became a legal proof by consensus. It then asserts that the usuli methodology grew organically, especially in Iraq, and it is incorrect to attribute its development solely to the influence of Aristotelian logic translated into Arabic and Persian. Instead, the methodology adopted and shared methods with the mutakallimun (theologians). The author cites Imam al-Haramayn, al-Zarkashi, and al-Iji to support the mutual influence between usuliyyun and mutakallimun. Al-Iji is quoted as saying that rational proofs are more connected to fiqh than to kalam, and the topic of 'al-hadd al-usuli' (the usuli definition) is more attributed to usul scholars. The passage then discusses the Hanafi school's approach of building usul from furu', whereas al-Shafi'i reversed this by establishing furu' on usul. The narrative culminates with al-Shafi'i's systematic contribution: he analyzed the qiyas methodology, organized it, added rhetorical investigations, and established the branches of his madhhab on firm usul. Two quotes support this: al-Razi praises al-Shafi'i for creating a universal law for legal evidence, and Mustafa 'Abd al-Raziq notes al-Shafi'i's synthetic and philosophical method in deducing rulings. The passage emphasizes the interdependence of kalam and usul and credits al-Shafi'i with systematizing the field.

Key Terms
الشافعي
القياس
المنهج الأصولي
المباحث البيانية

B) Hanafis established usul from furu', while al-Shafi'i established furu' from usul

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's genius lay in reversing the direction of deduction, creating a top-down universal legal methodology from principles to branches.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Two Schools of Usul al-Fiqh and Their Independence from Aristotelian Logic
Author divides usul scholars and notes both schools avoided Aristotelian logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the fuqaha' and mutakallimun schools of usul al-fiqh and identify evidence that both avoided Aristotelian logic.

Core Idea
Early usul scholars built Islamic legal theory independently, without relying on Greek logic.

Understanding the historical division of usul al-fiqh into two schools—the jurist legal theorists and the theologian legal theorists—is essential for grasping the development of Islamic legal reasoning. This lesson outlines the key features, figures, and works of each school, and highlights a crucial fact: both schools developed their methods free from Aristotelian influence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main schools
Read the passage and note the two categories: 'al-usuliyyin al-fuqaha'' (jurist usulis) and 'al-usuliyyin al-mutakallimin' (theologian usulis).
2
List key figures and works for the fuqaha' school
From the passage, extract the names of scholars and their books that represent the fuqaha' school: al-Dabusi, al-Bazdawi, Ibn al-Sa'ati, al-Shatibi, al-Qarafi, al-Subki, and their respective works.
Notice that the author emphasizes these works are 'free from Aristotelian influence.'
3
List key figures and works for the mutakallimun school
Do the same for the mutakallimun school: note the Ash'ari and Mu'tazila scholars mentioned (al-Baqillani, Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar, Abu al-Husayn al-Basri, Abu Hashim al-Jubbai') and the comment that their texts follow a dialectical style, not Aristotelian.
The author states these texts 'were not placed in an Aristotelian manner.'
4
Compare the methods of the two schools
The fuqaha' mixed usul with fiqh, using many examples and building general rules on juristic subtleties. The mutakallimun abstracted general rules rationally, using kalam methods and theoretical demonstration.
Both used qiyas (analogical reasoning) but in different styles.
5
Confirm the shared rejection of Aristotelian logic
The author explicitly says both schools' works are free from Aristotelian logic. This is a key historical claim that challenges later assumptions about Islamic borrowing from Greek logic.
This independence is illustrated by the fact that early usul works do not employ Aristotelian syllogisms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأساس يمكننا تقسيم علماء الأصول إلى قسمين : الأصوليين الفقهاء والأصوليين المتكلمين . أما الأول فقد امتزجت في كتاباتهم الأصول بالفقه وكثر تفريع المسائل الجزئية وذكر الأمثلة والشواهد ـ وبنيت المسائل الكلية العامة على النكت الفقهية ـ ويمثل هذا القسم فقهاء الحنفية ، ومن أئمتهم المتقدمين الدبوسي ( ٤٣٠ هـ ) وقد كتب في القياس بأوسع ممن كان قبله وتمم مباحثه وشرائطه ـ وكان له أكبر الأثر في المعاونة على إكمال المنهج الفقهي (١) ـ وكتابه هو تأسيس النظر . ثم كتب البزدوي كتاباً مطولاً ـ كشف الأسرار ـ ثم جمع ابن الساعاتي (٢) ( ٦١٤ هـ ) بين طريقة المتكلمين والفقهاء مستنداً إلى كتابي الأحكام للآمدي وكشف الأسرار للبزدوي في كتاب سماه « بدائع النظام » ثم كتب الإمام الشاطبي ( ٧٩٠ هـ ) كتاب الموافقات ، وسار أيضاً على هذا النهج شهاب الدين القرافي ( ٦٨٤ هـ ) وله كتاب الذخيرة ، وكتاب أنوار البروق في نواء الفروق ، ثم كتب السبكي كتابه المشهور « جمع الجوامع » وقد اقتصر ابن السبكي في هذا الكتاب على ذكر مسائل الأصول مجردة من الأدلة والشواهد ، وقد شرح هذا الكتاب شروحاً عدة كان أهمها شرح المحلي (٣) ( ٧٦١ هـ ٨٦٤ م ) وشرح الزركشي ( ٧٩٤ هـ ) . وهذه الكتب كلها بين أيدينا وقد خلت من أي تأثير بالمنطق الأرسططاليسي .
أما القسم الثاني وهم المتكلمون أشاعرة كانوا أو معتزلة (٤) . وهنا نرى محاولة عقلية بحتة تقوم على تجريد القواعد العامة من المسائل الفقهية وتستند في هذا إلى الاستدلال العقلي والبرهنة النظرية (٥) . فاستخدمت طرق البحث الكلامية أو مدارك العقول التي عرفت قبل الشافعي في المدرسة الأصولية الكلامية . ووضعت تلك الطرق وخاصة طريق القياس في صورة عقلية مجردة . ودخلت أبحاث كلامية كثيرة لما كان علم الكلام معتبراً واحداً من مصادر هذا العلم الثلاثة ، لا لدى المتكلمين وحدهم بل ولدى الفقهاء حتى الظاهرية منهم . أما عن المعتزلة فكما أنه لم تصل إلينا كتبهم في علم الكلام ، لم تصل الينا كتبهم في علم الأصول ، وخاصة كتاب العهد للقاضي عبد الجبار ( ٤١٥ هـ ) وشرحه المعتمد لأبي الحسين البصري ( ٤٣٦ هـ ) ومع ذلك يمكننا أن نستخلص جوهر الأصول المعتزلية وعلى الخصوص لدى أبي هاشم الجبائي مفكر المعتزلة العظيم - من كتب المتأخرين من أهل السنة - وسيكون هذا محل دراسة أخرى خاصة . ودراسة هذه النصوص تشعر تماماً بأنها لم توضع على طريقة الأرسططاليسيين ، بل على طريقة الجدليين من نظار المسلمين .
أما الأشاعرة فقد احترزوا أيضاً بأصولهم عن منطق أرسطو ، ونجد هذا واضحاً لدى عدو ممتاز للتراث اليوناني - أبي بكر الباقلاني - وهي شخصية ضخمة لم تبحث بعد - ولم تصل إلينا إنتاجها الأصولي إلا خلال كتب المتأخرين أيضاً .
In principle, we can divide the scholars of usul into two types: the jurist usulis and the theologian usulis. As for the first, in their writings usul was mixed with fiqh, and the detailed subsidiary issues and examples and evidences multiplied, and the general universal issues were built upon juristic subtleties. This type is represented by the Hanafi jurists. Among their early imams is al-Dabusi (430 AH) who wrote on qiyas more extensively than those before him and completed its topics and conditions, and he had the greatest impact in helping to complete the juristic methodology, and his book is Ta'sis al-Nazar. Then al-Bazdawi wrote a lengthy book Kashf al-Asrar. Then Ibn al-Sa'ati (614 AH) combined the method of the theologians and jurists, relying on the two books al-Ahkam by al-Amidi and Kashf al-Asrar by al-Bazdawi, in a book he called Bada'i' al-Nizam. Then Imam al-Shatibi (790 AH) wrote al-Muwafaqat, and Shihab al-Din al-Qarafi (684 AH) also followed this path, for he has the book al-Dhakhira and the book Anwar al-Buruq fi Anwa' al-Furuq. Then al-Subki wrote his famous book Jam' al-Jawami', and Ibn al-Subki limited himself in this book to mentioning the issues of usul stripped of evidences and proofs. This book has several commentaries, the most important being the commentary of al-Mahalli (761 AH/864 CE) and the commentary of al-Zarkashi (794 AH). All these books are in our hands and they are free from any influence of Aristotelian logic. As for the second type, they are the theologians, whether Ash'aris or Mu'tazila. Here we see a purely rational attempt based on abstracting general rules from juristic issues and relying on rational inference and theoretical demonstration. So they used the methods of kalam or intellectual perceptions that were known before al-Shafi'i in the theological usul school. They placed those methods, especially the method of qiyas, in an abstract rational form. Many kalam investigations entered because kalam was considered one of the three sources of this science, not only for theologians but also for jurists, even the Zahiris among them. As for the Mu'tazila, just as their books on kalam have not reached us, their books on usul have not reached us either, especially the book al-'Ahd by Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar (415 AH) and its commentary al-Mu'tamad by Abu al-Husayn al-Basri (436 AH). Yet we can extract the essence of Mu'tazili usul, especially from Abu Hashim al-Jubbai', the great thinker of the Mu'tazila, from the books of later Sunni scholars, and this will be the subject of a separate study. Studying these texts fully reveals that they were not placed in an Aristotelian manner, but in the manner of the dialecticians (jadaliyyun) among Muslim theoreticians. As for the Ash'aris, they also guarded their usul from Aristotelian logic, and we find this clearly in a distinguished enemy of Greek heritage, Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, a great figure that has not yet been researched, and his usul production has not reached us except through the books of later scholars as well.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a historical classification of usul al-fiqh scholars into two main schools: the jurist usulis and the theologian usulis. The author begins by stating this division. He then describes the first school, the fuqaha' usulis, exemplified by the Hanafi jurists. He lists several key figures and works: al-Dabusi (Ta'sis al-Nazar), al-Bazdawi (Kashf al-Asrar), Ibn al-Sa'ati (Bada'i' al-Nizam), al-Shatibi (al-Muwafaqat), al-Qarafi (al-Dhakhira), and al-Subki (Jam' al-Jawami'). The hallmark of this school is the integration of fiqh with usul, frequent citation of subsidiary issues and examples, and building general principles on juristic subtleties. Crucially, the author notes that all these works are free from Aristotelian logic. Next, the author turns to the second school, the mutakallimun usulis, whether Ash'ari or Mu'tazila. Their approach is characterized by pure rational abstraction, deriving general rules from juristic issues using rational inference and theoretical demonstration, not juristic examples. They employed the methods of kalam, particularly in their treatment of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author then discusses the Mu'tazila specifically, lamenting the loss of their original works but noting that their essential usul can be extracted from later Sunni writings. He emphasizes that these texts were not composed in an Aristotelian style but in the dialectical style of Muslim theorists. Finally, he addresses the Ash'aris, highlighting al-Baqillani as a prominent enemy of Greek heritage, though his usul works are also only known through later sources. Overall, the author establishes that both early schools avoided Aristotelian logic, setting the stage for a later shift.

الأصوليين المتكلمين
المنطق الأرسططاليسي
القياس

Key Takeaway
Early usul al-fiqh scholars, both jurist and theologian, developed their methods independently of Aristotelian logic, as demonstrated by the works of al-Dabusi, al-Baqillani, and others.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Early Islamic Legal Theory and Its Resistance to Aristotelian Logic
Author presents early resistance to Greek logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the methodological independence of early usul al-fiqh from Aristotelian logic.

Core Idea
Early usul al-fiqh developed dialectically, not aristotelically.

Before al-Ghazali, Islamic legal theory was shaped by dialectical methods (jadal) rather than Aristotelian logic. This lesson explores how early scholars, both Mu'tazila and Ash'ari, guarded their discipline against Greek influence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pre-Shafi'i theological-usul school
Find in the passage the description of methods known before al-Shafi'i. Note that they placed qiyas in an abstract intellectual form.
2
Analyze the Mu'tazila's method
The passage states that Mu'tazili texts were not Aristotelian but dialectical. Look for the name of Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i as a key figure.
3
Examine Ash'ari resistance
Abu Bakr al-Baqillani is described as an 'excellent opponent' of Greek logic. His works have come through later books.
4
Summarize the dominant method
Conclude that early usul followed a dialectical approach, not Aristotelian formal logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلامية أو مدارك العقول التي عرفت قبل الشافعي في المدرسة الأصولية الكلامية . ووضعت تلك الطرق وخاصة طريق القياس في صورة عقلية مجردة . ودخلت أبحاث كلامية كثيرة لما كان علم الكلام معتبراً واحداً من مصادر هذا العلم الثلاثة ، لا لدى المتكلمين وحدهم بل ولدى الفقهاء حتى الظاهرية منهم . أما عن المعتزلة فكما أنه لم تصل إلينا كتبهم في علم الكلام ، لم تصل الينا كتبهم في علم الأصول ، وخاصة كتاب العهد للقاضي عبد الجبار ( ٤١٥ هـ ) وشرحه المعتمد لأبي الحسين البصري ( ٤٣٦ هـ ) ومع ذلك يمكننا أن نستخلص جوهر الأصول المعتزلية وعلى الخصوص لدى أبي هاشم الجبائي مفكر المعتزلة العظيم - من كتب المتأخرين من أهل السنة - وسيكون هذا محل دراسة أخرى خاصة . ودراسة هذه النصوص تشعر تماماً بأنها لم توضع على طريقة الأرسططاليسيين ، بل على طريقة الجدليين من نظار المسلمين .
أما الأشاعرة فقد احترزوا أيضاً بأصولهم عن منطق أرسطو ، ونجد هذا واضحاً لدى عدو ممتاز للتراث اليوناني - أبي بكر الباقلاني - وهي شخصية ضخمة لم تبحث بعد - ولم تصل إلينا إنتاجها الأصولي إلا خلال كتب المتأخرين أيضاً .
ولكن ما لبث علم الأصول أن اتجه وجهة أخرى على يد امام الحرمين ( ٤٨٨ هـ ) وقد كان المظنون أن إمام الحرمين سار على منهج المدرسة الكلامية الأصولية الأولى - إلا أنه تسنى لي بحث مخطوطة نادرة لكتاب البرهان فتبين لي أنه وان كان إمام الحرمين خالف المنطق الأرسططاليسي في نقاط كثيرة ، إلا أنه تأثر به إلى حد كبير . بل قد نجد عنده أول محاولة لمزج منطق أرسطو بأصول الفقه . فكما أنه خالف متكلمي أهل السنة في القول بالواسطة أولاً(١) ، ثم وافق أبا هاشم الجبائي في أقوال له كثيرة(٢) يقول ابن تيمية عنه « واستمد من كلام أبي هاشم الجبائي على مختارات له ، ولقد خرج على طريقة القاضي وذويه في مواضع الى طريقة المعتزلة »(١) ثم انكاره علم الله بالجزئيات فكما أنه خالف الجمهور في كل هذا ، نراه يخالفهم أيضاً في محاولته مزج المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول . ويمهد الطريق بذلك لتلميذه أبي حامد الغزالي ، مما أدى الى مهاجمة السلف لهذا الأخير مهاجمة عنيفة قاسية .
ويعتبر الغزالي المازج الحقيقي للمنطق الأرسطاطاليسي بعلوم المسلمين . لا لما وضع من كتب منطقية سهلة العبارة ، بل لتلك المقدمة المنطقية التي وضعها في أول كتابه المستصفى ، والتي ذكر فيها أن من لا يحيط بها فلا ثقة بعلومه قطعاً . وعلى هذا الأساس اعتبر منطق أرسطو شرطاً من شروط الاجتهاد وفرض كفاية على المسلمين ، ووجهت إلى الغزالي بسبب هذا اعتراضات شديدة من فقهاء المسلمين .
ومنذ ذلك الحين بدأ الأصوليون المتكلمون يتأثرون بالمنطق الأرسططاليسي ويفردون في أول كتبهم فصلاً خاصاً لما أسموه « المقدمات الكلامية »(٢) أو « المقدمات الدخيلة » يلخصون فيها منطق أرسطو أو بمعنى أدق منطق الشراح الاسلاميين مشائياً تارة ورواقياً طوراً وكانت أكثر المباحث تأثراً بالمنطق اليوناني هذا ـ مباحث الألفاظ ـ أما مبحث القياس فقد استمر حتى بين أيدي الأصوليين المتأخرين بمنأى إلى أكبر حد عن هذا المنطق اليوناني أرسططاليسياً كان أو رواقياً .
ولن نعرض في هذه الفصول لتلك المقدمات الكلامية . فقد سبق أن عرضنا لجميع أنواع المنطق اليوناني بين أيدي شراحه الإسلاميين . وتلك المقدمات ليست إلا صورة من هذه الشروح الجمة التي كتبها الإسلاميون
Theological or rational perceptions that were known before al-Shafi'i in the theological-usul school. Those methods, especially the method of qiyas, were placed in an abstract intellectual form. Many theological investigations entered because the science of kalam was considered one of the three sources of this science, not only for the theologians but also for the jurists, even the Zahiris among them. As for the Mu'tazila, just as their books on kalam did not reach us, their books on usul did not reach us either, especially the book al-'Ahd by al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar (415 AH) and its commentary al-Mu'tamad by Abu al-Husayn al-Basri (436 AH). Nevertheless, we can extract the essence of Mu'tazili usul, particularly from Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i, the great Mu'tazili thinker, from the books of later Sunni scholars, and this will be the subject of another special study. Studying these texts fully gives the impression that they were not composed according to the Aristotelian method, but rather according to the dialectical method of Muslim theorists.
As for the Ash'aris, they also guarded their usul against Aristotle's logic, and we find this clearly in an excellent opponent of the Greek heritage, Abu Bakr al-Baqillani—a massive figure not yet studied—and his usul productions have reached us only through later books.
But soon usul al-fiqh took another direction at the hands of Imam al-Haramayn (488 AH). It was thought that Imam al-Haramayn followed the method of the first theological-usul school. However, I managed to examine a rare manuscript of his book al-Burhan, and it became clear to me that although Imam al-Haramayn differed from Aristotelian logic in many points, he was greatly influenced by it. Indeed, we find in him the first attempt to merge Aristotle's logic with usul al-fiqh. Just as he opposed the Sunni theologians in the doctrine of intermediacy first, then agreed with Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i in many of his statements, Ibn Taymiyya says about him: 'He drew from the speech of Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i based on his selected texts, and he departed from the method of al-Qadi and his followers in some places to the method of the Mu'tazila.' Then his denial of God's knowledge of particulars. So just as he opposed the majority in all this, we see him also opposing them in his attempt to merge Aristotelian logic with usul. By this, he paved the way for his student Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, which led the Salaf to attack the latter violently and harshly.
Al-Ghazali is considered the real merger of Aristotelian logic with the Islamic sciences—not because of the simplified logical books he wrote, but because of the logical introduction he placed at the beginning of his book al-Mustasfa, in which he stated that whoever does not master it, then his sciences are absolutely not reliable. On this basis, Aristotle's logic was considered a condition of ijtihad and a communal obligation upon Muslims, and al-Ghazali faced severe objections from Muslim jurists because of this.
From then on, the theologian-usul scholars began to be influenced by Aristotelian logic, and they set apart a special chapter at the beginning of their books for what they called 'theological introductions' or 'included introductions,' in which they summarized Aristotle's logic, or more precisely, the logic of Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic and sometimes Stoic. The most influenced topics by Greek logic were the topics of words. As for the topic of qiyas, it remained even in the hands of later usul scholars largely isolated from this Greek logic, whether Aristotelian or Stoic.
We will not present in these chapters those theological introductions. We have already presented all types of Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators. Those introductions are nothing but a form of these abundant commentaries written by Muslims.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of the relationship between Aristotelian logic and the Islamic discipline of usul al-fiqh (legal theory). The author begins by noting that before al-Shafi'i, there existed a theological-usul school that formulated methods of legal reasoning, especially qiyas (analogical deduction), in an abstract rational form. Theological investigations entered usul because kalam (scholastic theology) was one of its three sources, and this influenced both theologians and jurists, including the Zahiris who rejected analogical reasoning.

The author then discusses the Mu'tazila: their works on kalam and usul did not survive, but through later Sunni works we can extract the essence of Mu'tazili usul, especially from Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i. The author emphasizes that these texts were not Aristotelian but dialectical (jadal) in method.

Next, the Ash'aris are mentioned, particularly Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, who also resisted Aristotelian logic. However, a shift occurred with Imam al-Haramayn (d. 478 AH). Although initially thought to follow the early theological-usul school, examination of his manuscript al-Burhan reveals that despite his disagreements with Aristotelian logic on many points, he was significantly influenced and made the first attempt to merge it with usul al-fiqh. He also agreed with the Mu'tazila on some positions, such as denying God's knowledge of particulars, and this paved the way for his student al-Ghazali.

Al-Ghazali is presented as the real integrator of Aristotelian logic into Islamic sciences. Not just through his simplified logical works, but through the logical introduction to his usul work al-Mustasfa, where he made mastery of logic a prerequisite for reliable knowledge and a necessary condition for ijtihad, making it a communal obligation. This provoked strong opposition from traditionalist jurists.

After al-Ghazali, theologian-usul scholars routinely included a chapter on logic (called 'theological introductions' or 'included introductions') in their usul works, summarizing Aristotelian logic as interpreted by Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic, sometimes Stoic. The most influenced area was the study of words (alfaz), while the topic of qiyas itself remained relatively insulated from Greek logic.

The author concludes that he will not present those introductions in this book, as he has already covered Greek logic through its Islamic commentators, and those introductions are merely reproductions of those commentaries.

Key Terms
أصول الفقه
المنطق الأرسططاليسي
المقدمات الكلامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which method did early Mu'tazili and Ash'ari usul texts follow?
A) Aristotelian syllogistic
B) Dialectical (jadal)
C) Stoic logic
D) Peripatetic logic

Key Takeaway
Early usul al-fiqh was methodologically independent of Aristotelian logic, relying instead on dialectical reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Compare the presentation of qiyas in al-Jassas's al-Fusul fi al-Usul with the Aristotelian syllogism in later works by al-Ghazali. Identify elements of dialectic vs. syllogistic.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Shift: Imam al-Haramayn's Attempt to Merge Logic with Usul al-Fiqh
Author details Imam al-Haramayn's pioneering integration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how Imam al-Haramayn first attempted to integrate Aristotelian logic into usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Imam al-Haramayn made the first attempt to merge Aristotle's logic with usul.

Despite earlier resistance, Imam al-Haramayn (d. 478 AH) began incorporating elements of Aristotelian logic into his usul work al-Burhan. This lesson examines his role as a transitional figure who paved the way for al-Ghazali.

Guided Path
1
Identify the shift
Find the phrase indicating that usul took a different direction with Imam al-Haramayn. Note that his manuscript al-Burhan revealed his influence from Aristotelian logic.
2
Note his agreements with Mu'tazila
The passage mentions he agreed with Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i and deviated from the Ash'ari school. List the points: doctrine of intermediacy, denial of God's knowledge of particulars.
3
Recognize his merging attempt
He 'made the first attempt to merge Aristotle's logic with usul al-fiqh.' This is a key claim.
4
Assess his influence on al-Ghazali
He paved the way for his student al-Ghazali, leading to later controversies.

According to the passage, what did Imam al-Haramayn do that was unprecedented in usul al-fiqh?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Al-Ghazali: The Real Merger and Its Controversy
Author discusses al-Ghazali's integration and its aftermath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Ghazali's role as the real integrator of Aristotelian logic into Islamic sciences and why it sparked controversy.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali made logic a condition for ijtihad, triggering fierce opposition.

Al-Ghazali is described as the real merger of Aristotelian logic with Islamic sciences. By placing a logical introduction in his usul work al-Mustasfa and declaring logic a prerequisite for reliable knowledge, he sparked strong reactions from traditional jurists. This lesson examines his pivotal role and its aftermath.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Ghazali's contribution
He is called 'the real merger' (المازج الحقيقي). Note that his innovation was not just simplified logic books but the logical introduction to al-Mustasfa.
2
Understand his declaration
He stated that whoever does not master logic, his sciences are not reliable. This elevated logic to a condition of ijtihad and a communal obligation.
3
Recognize the opposition
The Salaf launched a violent and harsh attack against al-Ghazali because of this integration.
4
Describe the post-Ghazali trend
Theologian-usul scholars began including 'theological introductions' in their works, summarizing Aristotelian logic. Note that the topic of qiyas remained relatively insulated.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلامية أو مدارك العقول التي عرفت قبل الشافعي في المدرسة الأصولية الكلامية . ووضعت تلك الطرق وخاصة طريق القياس في صورة عقلية مجردة . ودخلت أبحاث كلامية كثيرة لما كان علم الكلام معتبراً واحداً من مصادر هذا العلم الثلاثة ، لا لدى المتكلمين وحدهم بل ولدى الفقهاء حتى الظاهرية منهم . أما عن المعتزلة فكما أنه لم تصل إلينا كتبهم في علم الكلام ، لم تصل الينا كتبهم في علم الأصول ، وخاصة كتاب العهد للقاضي عبد الجبار ( ٤١٥ هـ ) وشرحه المعتمد لأبي الحسين البصري ( ٤٣٦ هـ ) ومع ذلك يمكننا أن نستخلص جوهر الأصول المعتزلية وعلى الخصوص لدى أبي هاشم الجبائي مفكر المعتزلة العظيم - من كتب المتأخرين من أهل السنة - وسيكون هذا محل دراسة أخرى خاصة . ودراسة هذه النصوص تشعر تماماً بأنها لم توضع على طريقة الأرسططاليسيين ، بل على طريقة الجدليين من نظار المسلمين .
أما الأشاعرة فقد احترزوا أيضاً بأصولهم عن منطق أرسطو ، ونجد هذا واضحاً لدى عدو ممتاز للتراث اليوناني - أبي بكر الباقلاني - وهي شخصية ضخمة لم تبحث بعد - ولم تصل إلينا إنتاجها الأصولي إلا خلال كتب المتأخرين أيضاً .
ولكن ما لبث علم الأصول أن اتجه وجهة أخرى على يد امام الحرمين ( ٤٨٨ هـ ) وقد كان المظنون أن إمام الحرمين سار على منهج المدرسة الكلامية الأصولية الأولى - إلا أنه تسنى لي بحث مخطوطة نادرة لكتاب البرهان فتبين لي أنه وان كان إمام الحرمين خالف المنطق الأرسططاليسي في نقاط كثيرة ، إلا أنه تأثر به إلى حد كبير . بل قد نجد عنده أول محاولة لمزج منطق أرسطو بأصول الفقه . فكما أنه خالف متكلمي أهل السنة في القول بالواسطة أولاً(١) ، ثم وافق أبا هاشم الجبائي في أقوال له كثيرة(٢) يقول ابن تيمية عنه « واستمد من كلام أبي هاشم الجبائي على مختارات له ، ولقد خرج على طريقة القاضي وذويه في مواضع الى طريقة المعتزلة »(١) ثم انكاره علم الله بالجزئيات فكما أنه خالف الجمهور في كل هذا ، نراه يخالفهم أيضاً في محاولته مزج المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول . ويمهد الطريق بذلك لتلميذه أبي حامد الغزالي ، مما أدى الى مهاجمة السلف لهذا الأخير مهاجمة عنيفة قاسية .
ويعتبر الغزالي المازج الحقيقي للمنطق الأرسطاطاليسي بعلوم المسلمين . لا لما وضع من كتب منطقية سهلة العبارة ، بل لتلك المقدمة المنطقية التي وضعها في أول كتابه المستصفى ، والتي ذكر فيها أن من لا يحيط بها فلا ثقة بعلومه قطعاً . وعلى هذا الأساس اعتبر منطق أرسطو شرطاً من شروط الاجتهاد وفرض كفاية على المسلمين ، ووجهت إلى الغزالي بسبب هذا اعتراضات شديدة من فقهاء المسلمين .
ومنذ ذلك الحين بدأ الأصوليون المتكلمون يتأثرون بالمنطق الأرسططاليسي ويفردون في أول كتبهم فصلاً خاصاً لما أسموه « المقدمات الكلامية »(٢) أو « المقدمات الدخيلة » يلخصون فيها منطق أرسطو أو بمعنى أدق منطق الشراح الاسلاميين مشائياً تارة ورواقياً طوراً وكانت أكثر المباحث تأثراً بالمنطق اليوناني هذا ـ مباحث الألفاظ ـ أما مبحث القياس فقد استمر حتى بين أيدي الأصوليين المتأخرين بمنأى إلى أكبر حد عن هذا المنطق اليوناني أرسططاليسياً كان أو رواقياً .
ولن نعرض في هذه الفصول لتلك المقدمات الكلامية . فقد سبق أن عرضنا لجميع أنواع المنطق اليوناني بين أيدي شراحه الإسلاميين . وتلك المقدمات ليست إلا صورة من هذه الشروح الجمة التي كتبها الإسلاميون
Theological or rational perceptions that were known before al-Shafi'i in the theological-usul school. Those methods, especially the method of qiyas, were placed in an abstract intellectual form. Many theological investigations entered because the science of kalam was considered one of the three sources of this science, not only for the theologians but also for the jurists, even the Zahiris among them. As for the Mu'tazila, just as their books on kalam did not reach us, their books on usul did not reach us either, especially the book al-'Ahd by al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar (415 AH) and its commentary al-Mu'tamad by Abu al-Husayn al-Basri (436 AH). Nevertheless, we can extract the essence of Mu'tazili usul, particularly from Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i, the great Mu'tazili thinker, from the books of later Sunni scholars, and this will be the subject of another special study. Studying these texts fully gives the impression that they were not composed according to the Aristotelian method, but rather according to the dialectical method of Muslim theorists.
As for the Ash'aris, they also guarded their usul against Aristotle's logic, and we find this clearly in an excellent opponent of the Greek heritage, Abu Bakr al-Baqillani—a massive figure not yet studied—and his usul productions have reached us only through later books.
But soon usul al-fiqh took another direction at the hands of Imam al-Haramayn (488 AH). It was thought that Imam al-Haramayn followed the method of the first theological-usul school. However, I managed to examine a rare manuscript of his book al-Burhan, and it became clear to me that although Imam al-Haramayn differed from Aristotelian logic in many points, he was greatly influenced by it. Indeed, we find in him the first attempt to merge Aristotle's logic with usul al-fiqh. Just as he opposed the Sunni theologians in the doctrine of intermediacy first, then agreed with Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i in many of his statements, Ibn Taymiyya says about him: 'He drew from the speech of Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i based on his selected texts, and he departed from the method of al-Qadi and his followers in some places to the method of the Mu'tazila.' Then his denial of God's knowledge of particulars. So just as he opposed the majority in all this, we see him also opposing them in his attempt to merge Aristotelian logic with usul. By this, he paved the way for his student Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, which led the Salaf to attack the latter violently and harshly.
Al-Ghazali is considered the real merger of Aristotelian logic with the Islamic sciences—not because of the simplified logical books he wrote, but because of the logical introduction he placed at the beginning of his book al-Mustasfa, in which he stated that whoever does not master it, then his sciences are absolutely not reliable. On this basis, Aristotle's logic was considered a condition of ijtihad and a communal obligation upon Muslims, and al-Ghazali faced severe objections from Muslim jurists because of this.
From then on, the theologian-usul scholars began to be influenced by Aristotelian logic, and they set apart a special chapter at the beginning of their books for what they called 'theological introductions' or 'included introductions,' in which they summarized Aristotle's logic, or more precisely, the logic of Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic and sometimes Stoic. The most influenced topics by Greek logic were the topics of words. As for the topic of qiyas, it remained even in the hands of later usul scholars largely isolated from this Greek logic, whether Aristotelian or Stoic.
We will not present in these chapters those theological introductions. We have already presented all types of Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators. Those introductions are nothing but a form of these abundant commentaries written by Muslims.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of the relationship between Aristotelian logic and the Islamic discipline of usul al-fiqh (legal theory). The author begins by noting that before al-Shafi'i, there existed a theological-usul school that formulated methods of legal reasoning, especially qiyas (analogical deduction), in an abstract rational form. Theological investigations entered usul because kalam (scholastic theology) was one of its three sources, and this influenced both theologians and jurists, including the Zahiris who rejected analogical reasoning.

The author then discusses the Mu'tazila: their works on kalam and usul did not survive, but through later Sunni works we can extract the essence of Mu'tazili usul, especially from Abu Hashim al-Jubba'i. The author emphasizes that these texts were not Aristotelian but dialectical (jadal) in method.

Next, the Ash'aris are mentioned, particularly Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, who also resisted Aristotelian logic. However, a shift occurred with Imam al-Haramayn (d. 478 AH). Although initially thought to follow the early theological-usul school, examination of his manuscript al-Burhan reveals that despite his disagreements with Aristotelian logic on many points, he was significantly influenced and made the first attempt to merge it with usul al-fiqh. He also agreed with the Mu'tazila on some positions, such as denying God's knowledge of particulars, and this paved the way for his student al-Ghazali.

Al-Ghazali is presented as the real integrator of Aristotelian logic into Islamic sciences. Not just through his simplified logical works, but through the logical introduction to his usul work al-Mustasfa, where he made mastery of logic a prerequisite for reliable knowledge and a necessary condition for ijtihad, making it a communal obligation. This provoked strong opposition from traditionalist jurists.

After al-Ghazali, theologian-usul scholars routinely included a chapter on logic (called 'theological introductions' or 'included introductions') in their usul works, summarizing Aristotelian logic as interpreted by Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic, sometimes Stoic. The most influenced area was the study of words (alfaz), while the topic of qiyas itself remained relatively insulated from Greek logic.

The author concludes that he will not present those introductions in this book, as he has already covered Greek logic through its Islamic commentators, and those introductions are merely reproductions of those commentaries.

Key Terms
الغزالي
المستصفى
المقدمات الكلامية

B) He rejected the use of qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali's integration of Aristotelian logic into usul al-fiqh, by making it a prerequisite for ijtihad, was a turning point that provoked strong opposition but also became a lasting feature of the discipline.

Introduction and Front Matter

Early Mixing: Abu Hashim al-Jubbai
Author traces early mixing by al-Jubbai.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the early attempt of Abu Hashim al-Jubbai to integrate Aristotelian logic with usul and explain how it paved the way for al-Ghazali.

Core Idea
Al-Jubbai's mixing of logic into usul was a precursor to Ghazali's fuller integration.

The integration of Aristotelian logic into Islamic usul al-fiqh did not happen overnight. The passage points to Abu Hashim al-Jubbai as an early figure who attempted this mixing, though his efforts were part of a broader departure from mainstream positions. Understanding his role helps us see the gradual nature of this development and the controversies it sparked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key figure
Locate the name 'Abu Hashim al-Jubbai' in the Arabic passage. Note that he is described as deriving from the speech of someone else (likely a teacher) and departing from the method of the judge (al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar) towards Mu'tazilite positions.
His departure in theology is linked to his attempt to mix logic with usul.
2
Identify the theological context
The passage mentions his denial of God's knowledge of particulars. This is a theological point that set him apart from the majority. Observe how the author connects this to his mixing of logic.
This shows that the mixing was not isolated but part of a broader intellectual stance.
3
Connect to al-Ghazali
The text says he 'paved the way' for his student Abu Hamid al-Ghazali. Reflect on how an early attempt, though opposed, prepared the ground for a more influential figure.
Al-Ghazali is later described as the 'true mixer'.

« واستمد من كلام أبي هاشم الجبائي على مختارات له ، ولقد خرج على طريقة القاضي وذويه في مواضع الى طريقة المعتزلة »(۱) ثم انكاره علم الله بالجزئيات فكما أنه خالف الجمهور في كل هذا ، نراه يخالفهم أيضاً في محاولته مزج المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول . ويمهد الطريق بذلك لتلميذه أبي حامد الغزالي ، مما أدى الى مهاجمة السلف لهذا الأخير مهاجمة عنيفة قاسية . ويعتبر الغزالي المازج الحقيقي للمنطق الأرسطاطاليسي بعلوم المسلمين . لا لما وضع من كتب منطقية سهلة العبارة ، بل لتلك المقدمة المنطقية التي وضعها في أول كتابه المستصفى ، والتي ذكر فيها أن من لا يحيط بها فلا ثقة بعلومه قطعاً . وعلى هذا الأساس اعتبر منطق أرسطو شرطاً من شروط الاجتهاد وفرض كفاية على المسلمين ، ووجهت إلى الغزالي بسبب هذا اعتراضات شديدة من فقهاء المسلمين . ومنذ ذلك الحين بدأ الأصوليون المتكلمون يتأثرون بالمنطق الأرسططاليسي ويفردون في أول كتبهم فصلاً خاصاً لما أسموه « المقدمات الكلامية »(۲) أو « المقدمات الدخيلة » يلخصون فيها منطق أرسطو أو بمعنى أدق منطق الشراح الاسلاميين مشائياً تارة ورواقياً طوراً وكانت أكثر المباحث تأثراً بالمنطق اليوناني هذا ـ مباحث الألفاظ ـ أما مبحث القياس فقد استمر حتى بين أيدي الأصوليين المتأخرين بمنأى إلى أكبر حد عن هذا المنطق اليوناني أرسططاليسياً كان أو رواقياً . ولن نعرض في هذه الفصول لتلك المقدمات الكلامية . فقد سبق أن عرضنا لجميع أنواع المنطق اليوناني بين أيدي شراحه الإسلاميين . وتلك المقدمات ليست إلا صورة من هذه الشروح الجمة التي كتبها الإسلاميون والتي حللت عناصرها في الباب السابق . ولكن سنعرض لهذا المنهج الأصولي الكلامي - لأن المتكلمين يتشاركون فيه ، كما سنرى بعد ـ كما عرف قبل القرن الخامس . ولن أخوض في الأبحاث اللغوية لخروجها عن نطاق هذا البحث ، مع ملاحظة أن المباحث الأصولية اللغوية ليست من نوع علوم اللغة أو النحو العادية . فقد دقق الأصوليون نظرهم في فهم أشياء من كلام العرب لم يتوصل إليها اللغويون أو النحاة . إن كلام العرب متسع وطرق البحث فيه متشعبة . فكتب اللغة تضبط الألفاظ والمعاني الظاهرة دون المعاني الدقيقة التي يتوصل إليها الأصولي باستقراء يزيد على استقراء اللغوي . فهناك إذن دقائق لا يتعرض لها اللغوي ولا تقتضيها صناعة النحو . ولكن يتوصل إليها الأصوليون باستقراء خاص وأدلة خاصة(١) . هذا هو تاريخ المنهج الأصولي - استطعنا أن نتبين من خلاله موقف علماء أصول الفقه من المنطق الأرسططاليسي ، وتكون هذا المنهج منذ العصر الأول واستمر الأصوليون يكملون فيه ويضيفون إلى عناصره جدة في التفكير ، حتى وصل إلى أيدي الشافعي . فأقامه علماً متفق الأجزاء متناسق الأطراف . وفي كل هذا لم يتأثر على الإطلاق بمناهج البحث اليونانية - ثم انقسم إلى قسمين بعد الشافعي : علم الأصول الفقهي وعلم الأصول الكلامي . وفي كلا القسمين لم يتأثر أيضاً بمنطق أرسطو - حتى أتى القرن الخامس فمزج المسلمون المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول ، وبهذا انتهى أو كاد ينتهي تفكير المسلمين المبدع في المنطق . هذا هو موقف علماء أصول الفقه - فقهاء كانوا أو متكلمين . فما هو موقف علماء أصول الدين المتكلمين من المنطق الأرسططاليسي ؟ هذا ما سنبحثه في الفصل القادم .
And he derived from the speech of Abu Hashim al-Jubbai on his selections, and indeed he departed from the method of the judge and his followers in places to the method of the Mu'tazila. Then his denial of God's knowledge of particulars, so just as he opposed the majority in all this, we see him also opposing them in his attempt to mix Aristotelian logic with usul. And he thereby paved the way for his student Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, which led to the predecessors attacking this latter one with a violent, harsh attack. And al-Ghazali is considered the true mixer of Aristotelian logic with the sciences of the Muslims. Not for what he wrote of easy-expressed logical books, but for that logical introduction which he placed at the beginning of his book al-Mustasfa, in which he mentioned that whoever does not encompass it, then his knowledge is definitely not trusted. And on this basis, Aristotle's logic was considered a condition for ijtihad and a collective obligation upon the Muslims, and due to this, severe objections were directed at al-Ghazali from the Muslim jurists. And from that time, the usuli theologians began to be influenced by Aristotelian logic and set apart in the beginnings of their books a special chapter for what they called 'theological introductions' or 'incoming introductions' in which they summarized Aristotle's logic or, more precisely, the logic of the Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic and sometimes Stoic. And the most influenced by this Greek logic were the topics of words. As for the topic of qiyas, it continued, even in the hands of the later usulis, to be as far as possible from this Greek logic, whether Aristotelian or Stoic. And we will not present in these chapters those theological introductions. For we have already presented all types of Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators. And those introductions are nothing but a form of these numerous commentaries written by the Muslims, whose elements I analyzed in the previous chapter. But we will present this usuli-kalami methodology – because the theologians share in it, as we will see later – as it was known before the fifth century. And I will not delve into linguistic researches because they are outside the scope of this study, noting that the linguistic usuli researches are not of the type of ordinary language sciences or grammar. For the usulis examined their view in understanding things from Arab speech that the linguists or grammarians did not arrive at. Indeed, Arab speech is vast and the methods of research in it are diverse. Language books record the apparent words and meanings without the precise meanings that the usuli arrives at through an induction that goes beyond the linguist's induction. So there are subtleties that the linguist does not address and that the craft of grammar does not require. But the usulis arrive at them through special induction and special evidence. This is the history of the usuli methodology – we were able to discern from it the position of the scholars of usul al-fiqh towards Aristotelian logic, that this methodology was formed since the first era and the usulis continued completing it and adding to its elements novelty in thinking, until it reached the hands of al-Shafi'i. So he established it as a science of consistent parts and coherent limbs. And in all this it was not influenced at all by Greek methods of study – then it split after al-Shafi'i into two branches: the science of fiqhi usul and the science of kalami usul. And in both branches it was also not influenced by Aristotle's logic – until the fifth century came and the Muslims mixed Aristotelian logic with usul, and with this ended, or almost ended, the creative thinking of the Muslims in logic. This is the position of the scholars of usul al-fiqh – whether jurists or theologians. So what is the position of the scholars of usul al-din (theologians) regarding Aristotelian logic? This is what we will research in the next chapter.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of the relationship between Aristotelian logic and the Islamic science of usul al-fiqh. The author begins by mentioning Abu Hashim al-Jubbai, who attempted to mix logic with usul, and notes his departure from the method of the judge (likely al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar) and his followers towards Mu'tazilite positions. He also denied God's knowledge of particulars, which placed him in opposition to the majority. The author then highlights al-Ghazali as the true mixer of Aristotelian logic with Islamic sciences, not merely through his simplified logical writings but because of the logical introduction he placed at the beginning of his work 'al-Mustasfa', where he declared that anyone who does not master logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge. This elevated Aristotelian logic to a condition for ijtihad and a collective obligation (fard kifaya). This provoked strong opposition from jurists. Subsequently, usuli theologians began to incorporate a chapter called 'theological introductions' (al-muqaddimat al-kalamiyya) or 'incoming introductions' in their works, summarizing Aristotle's logic as interpreted by Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic, sometimes Stoic. The most affected area was the study of words (alfaz), while the study of analogy (qiyas) remained largely untouched by Greek logic. The author notes that he will not cover those theological introductions here, as he has already analyzed Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators in a previous chapter. Instead, he will present the usuli-kalami methodology as it existed before the fifth Islamic century. He then addresses the distinct nature of linguistic usul researches, which go beyond ordinary language sciences and grammar; usulis have developed their own inductive methods to grasp subtle meanings not accessible to linguists. The passage concludes by summarizing the history: usul methodology was formed early and developed independently, was systematized by al-Shafi'i without Greek influence, split into fiqhi and kalami usul, still without Aristotelian influence until the fifth century when mixing occurred, which the author views as potentially stifling creative thinking. The passage ends by promising a discussion on the attitude of kalam theologians (usul al-din) towards Aristotelian logic in the next chapter.

المقدمة المنطقية

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Al-Ghazali's Integration: Logic as a Prerequisite
Author discusses Ghazali's role and the objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze al-Ghazali's claim that mastery of Aristotelian logic is necessary for reliable knowledge and ijtihad, and explain the objections it raised.

Core Idea
Ghazali's logical introduction in al-Mustasfa made logic fard kifaya and a condition for ijtihad.

The passage identifies Abu Hamid al-Ghazali as the 'true mixer' of Aristotelian logic with Islamic sciences. His logical introduction in al-Mustasfa was not merely pedagogical; it declared that anyone lacking logic cannot be trusted in their knowledge. This elevated Aristotle's logic to a prerequisite for ijtihad, provoking strong objections from jurists. Understanding this shift is crucial for grasping the later integration of logic into usul.

Guided Path
1
Locate al-Ghazali's key contribution
In the Arabic, find where the author says 'wa yu' tabaru al-Ghazali al-mazij al-haqiqi'. Note that the author distinguishes between his easy logical writings and his logical introduction in al-Mustasfa. Focus on the latter as the main innovation.
The phrase 'man la yuhiitu biha fa la thiqata bi 'ulumihi qat' an' is the crucial claim.
2
Extract the logical requirement
The passage says that on this basis, Aristotle's logic was considered a condition (shart) for ijtihad and a collective obligation (fard kifaya). Write down these two consequences.
This is a major expansion of the role of logic; previously, ijtihad relied on mastery of Arabic, Quran, Sunna, and qiyas.
3
Identify the objections
Note the phrase 'shadida min fuqaha' al-muslimin' (severe objections from Muslim jurists). Why would jurists object? Consider how this requirement could exclude many qualified scholars.
The objections are part of the broader resistance to mixing logic with religious sciences.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
« واستمد من كلام أبي هاشم الجبائي على مختارات له ، ولقد خرج على طريقة القاضي وذويه في مواضع الى طريقة المعتزلة »(۱) ثم انكاره علم الله بالجزئيات فكما أنه خالف الجمهور في كل هذا ، نراه يخالفهم أيضاً في محاولته مزج المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول . ويمهد الطريق بذلك لتلميذه أبي حامد الغزالي ، مما أدى الى مهاجمة السلف لهذا الأخير مهاجمة عنيفة قاسية . ويعتبر الغزالي المازج الحقيقي للمنطق الأرسطاطاليسي بعلوم المسلمين . لا لما وضع من كتب منطقية سهلة العبارة ، بل لتلك المقدمة المنطقية التي وضعها في أول كتابه المستصفى ، والتي ذكر فيها أن من لا يحيط بها فلا ثقة بعلومه قطعاً . وعلى هذا الأساس اعتبر منطق أرسطو شرطاً من شروط الاجتهاد وفرض كفاية على المسلمين ، ووجهت إلى الغزالي بسبب هذا اعتراضات شديدة من فقهاء المسلمين . ومنذ ذلك الحين بدأ الأصوليون المتكلمون يتأثرون بالمنطق الأرسططاليسي ويفردون في أول كتبهم فصلاً خاصاً لما أسموه « المقدمات الكلامية »(۲) أو « المقدمات الدخيلة » يلخصون فيها منطق أرسطو أو بمعنى أدق منطق الشراح الاسلاميين مشائياً تارة ورواقياً طوراً وكانت أكثر المباحث تأثراً بالمنطق اليوناني هذا ـ مباحث الألفاظ ـ أما مبحث القياس فقد استمر حتى بين أيدي الأصوليين المتأخرين بمنأى إلى أكبر حد عن هذا المنطق اليوناني أرسططاليسياً كان أو رواقياً . ولن نعرض في هذه الفصول لتلك المقدمات الكلامية . فقد سبق أن عرضنا لجميع أنواع المنطق اليوناني بين أيدي شراحه الإسلاميين . وتلك المقدمات ليست إلا صورة من هذه الشروح الجمة التي كتبها الإسلاميون والتي حللت عناصرها في الباب السابق . ولكن سنعرض لهذا المنهج الأصولي الكلامي - لأن المتكلمين يتشاركون فيه ، كما سنرى بعد ـ كما عرف قبل القرن الخامس . ولن أخوض في الأبحاث اللغوية لخروجها عن نطاق هذا البحث ، مع ملاحظة أن المباحث الأصولية اللغوية ليست من نوع علوم اللغة أو النحو العادية . فقد دقق الأصوليون نظرهم في فهم أشياء من كلام العرب لم يتوصل إليها اللغويون أو النحاة . إن كلام العرب متسع وطرق البحث فيه متشعبة . فكتب اللغة تضبط الألفاظ والمعاني الظاهرة دون المعاني الدقيقة التي يتوصل إليها الأصولي باستقراء يزيد على استقراء اللغوي . فهناك إذن دقائق لا يتعرض لها اللغوي ولا تقتضيها صناعة النحو . ولكن يتوصل إليها الأصوليون باستقراء خاص وأدلة خاصة(١) . هذا هو تاريخ المنهج الأصولي - استطعنا أن نتبين من خلاله موقف علماء أصول الفقه من المنطق الأرسططاليسي ، وتكون هذا المنهج منذ العصر الأول واستمر الأصوليون يكملون فيه ويضيفون إلى عناصره جدة في التفكير ، حتى وصل إلى أيدي الشافعي . فأقامه علماً متفق الأجزاء متناسق الأطراف . وفي كل هذا لم يتأثر على الإطلاق بمناهج البحث اليونانية - ثم انقسم إلى قسمين بعد الشافعي : علم الأصول الفقهي وعلم الأصول الكلامي . وفي كلا القسمين لم يتأثر أيضاً بمنطق أرسطو - حتى أتى القرن الخامس فمزج المسلمون المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول ، وبهذا انتهى أو كاد ينتهي تفكير المسلمين المبدع في المنطق . هذا هو موقف علماء أصول الفقه - فقهاء كانوا أو متكلمين . فما هو موقف علماء أصول الدين المتكلمين من المنطق الأرسططاليسي ؟ هذا ما سنبحثه في الفصل القادم .
And he derived from the speech of Abu Hashim al-Jubbai on his selections, and indeed he departed from the method of the judge and his followers in places to the method of the Mu'tazila. Then his denial of God's knowledge of particulars, so just as he opposed the majority in all this, we see him also opposing them in his attempt to mix Aristotelian logic with usul. And he thereby paved the way for his student Abu Hamid al-Ghazali, which led to the predecessors attacking this latter one with a violent, harsh attack. And al-Ghazali is considered the true mixer of Aristotelian logic with the sciences of the Muslims. Not for what he wrote of easy-expressed logical books, but for that logical introduction which he placed at the beginning of his book al-Mustasfa, in which he mentioned that whoever does not encompass it, then his knowledge is definitely not trusted. And on this basis, Aristotle's logic was considered a condition for ijtihad and a collective obligation upon the Muslims, and due to this, severe objections were directed at al-Ghazali from the Muslim jurists. And from that time, the usuli theologians began to be influenced by Aristotelian logic and set apart in the beginnings of their books a special chapter for what they called 'theological introductions' or 'incoming introductions' in which they summarized Aristotle's logic or, more precisely, the logic of the Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic and sometimes Stoic. And the most influenced by this Greek logic were the topics of words. As for the topic of qiyas, it continued, even in the hands of the later usulis, to be as far as possible from this Greek logic, whether Aristotelian or Stoic. And we will not present in these chapters those theological introductions. For we have already presented all types of Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators. And those introductions are nothing but a form of these numerous commentaries written by the Muslims, whose elements I analyzed in the previous chapter. But we will present this usuli-kalami methodology – because the theologians share in it, as we will see later – as it was known before the fifth century. And I will not delve into linguistic researches because they are outside the scope of this study, noting that the linguistic usuli researches are not of the type of ordinary language sciences or grammar. For the usulis examined their view in understanding things from Arab speech that the linguists or grammarians did not arrive at. Indeed, Arab speech is vast and the methods of research in it are diverse. Language books record the apparent words and meanings without the precise meanings that the usuli arrives at through an induction that goes beyond the linguist's induction. So there are subtleties that the linguist does not address and that the craft of grammar does not require. But the usulis arrive at them through special induction and special evidence. This is the history of the usuli methodology – we were able to discern from it the position of the scholars of usul al-fiqh towards Aristotelian logic, that this methodology was formed since the first era and the usulis continued completing it and adding to its elements novelty in thinking, until it reached the hands of al-Shafi'i. So he established it as a science of consistent parts and coherent limbs. And in all this it was not influenced at all by Greek methods of study – then it split after al-Shafi'i into two branches: the science of fiqhi usul and the science of kalami usul. And in both branches it was also not influenced by Aristotle's logic – until the fifth century came and the Muslims mixed Aristotelian logic with usul, and with this ended, or almost ended, the creative thinking of the Muslims in logic. This is the position of the scholars of usul al-fiqh – whether jurists or theologians. So what is the position of the scholars of usul al-din (theologians) regarding Aristotelian logic? This is what we will research in the next chapter.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of the relationship between Aristotelian logic and the Islamic science of usul al-fiqh. The author begins by mentioning Abu Hashim al-Jubbai, who attempted to mix logic with usul, and notes his departure from the method of the judge (likely al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar) and his followers towards Mu'tazilite positions. He also denied God's knowledge of particulars, which placed him in opposition to the majority. The author then highlights al-Ghazali as the true mixer of Aristotelian logic with Islamic sciences, not merely through his simplified logical writings but because of the logical introduction he placed at the beginning of his work 'al-Mustasfa', where he declared that anyone who does not master logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge. This elevated Aristotelian logic to a condition for ijtihad and a collective obligation (fard kifaya). This provoked strong opposition from jurists. Subsequently, usuli theologians began to incorporate a chapter called 'theological introductions' (al-muqaddimat al-kalamiyya) or 'incoming introductions' in their works, summarizing Aristotle's logic as interpreted by Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic, sometimes Stoic. The most affected area was the study of words (alfaz), while the study of analogy (qiyas) remained largely untouched by Greek logic. The author notes that he will not cover those theological introductions here, as he has already analyzed Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators in a previous chapter. Instead, he will present the usuli-kalami methodology as it existed before the fifth Islamic century. He then addresses the distinct nature of linguistic usul researches, which go beyond ordinary language sciences and grammar; usulis have developed their own inductive methods to grasp subtle meanings not accessible to linguists. The passage concludes by summarizing the history: usul methodology was formed early and developed independently, was systematized by al-Shafi'i without Greek influence, split into fiqhi and kalami usul, still without Aristotelian influence until the fifth century when mixing occurred, which the author views as potentially stifling creative thinking. The passage ends by promising a discussion on the attitude of kalam theologians (usul al-din) towards Aristotelian logic in the next chapter.

Key Terms
الغزالي
المستصفى
شرط الاجتهاد
فرض كفاية

Checkpoint
What did al-Ghazali state in the logical introduction of al-Mustasfa?
A) Logic is useful but not necessary.
B) Whoever does not encompass it cannot be trusted in his knowledge.
C) Logic is only for philosophers, not jurists.
D) Ijtihad requires only knowledge of the Quran and Sunna.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali's logical introduction made Aristotelian logic a necessary condition for ijtihad and a collective obligation, sparking strong objections from jurists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a pre-Ghazali usul text (e.g., al-Shafi'i's al-Risala) and list the prerequisites for ijtihad. Then compare with al-Mustasfa. How does the addition of logic change the profile of a mujtahid?
?
Reflect on the objection of jurists: why might requiring logic for ijtihad be controversial? Consider the case of a scholar well-versed in Islamic sources but not in Aristotelian logic.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Theological Introductions and the Independence of Qiyas
Author discusses the theological introductions and the selective influence on usul topics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the influence of Aristotelian logic on the study of words (alfaz) and its lack of influence on legal analogy (qiyas) in usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
While theological introductions included logic, the core usul tool of qiyas remained independent.

After al-Ghazali, usuli theologians began to include a chapter called 'al-muqaddimat al-kalamiyya' summarizing Greek logic. However, the passage notes that these introductions impacted mainly the study of words (mabahith al-alfaz), while the topic of qiyas (legal analogy) remained largely untouched by both Aristotelian and Stoic logic. This selectivity shows that the integration of logic into usul was partial and strategic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the 'theological introductions'
Find the phrase 'al-muqaddimat al-kalamiyya' or 'al-muqaddimat al-dakhila' in the Arabic. Note that these are chapters summarizing Aristotle's logic as interpreted by Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic, sometimes Stoic.
These introductions became standard in later usul works.
2
Note the area most affected
The passage says 'wa kanat akthar al-mabahith ta'athuran bi al-mantiq al-yunani hadha – mabahith al-alfaz'. So the study of words (alfaz) was most influenced. Why might that be?
Aristotelian logic includes categories and predication, which relate to terms and definitions.
3
Observe the independence of qiyas
Contrast with the statement: 'amma mabahith al-qiyas fa qad istamarra ... bi man'an ila akbar hadd 'an hadha al-mantiq al-yunani'. Qiyas, the core of usul reasoning, remained far from Greek logic. This is a key point: usul's analogical reasoning was not replaced by syllogistic.
The author emphasizes this independence even among later usulis.

« واستمد من كلام أبي هاشم الجبائي على مختارات له ، ولقد خرج على طريقة القاضي وذويه في مواضع الى طريقة المعتزلة »(۱) ثم انكاره علم الله بالجزئيات فكما أنه خالف الجمهور في كل هذا ، نراه يخالفهم أيضاً في محاولته مزج المنطق الأرسططاليسي بالأصول . ويمهد الطريق بذلك لتلميذه أبي حامد الغزالي ، مما أدى الى مهاجمة السلف لهذا الأخير مهاجمة عنيفة قاسية . ويعتبر الغزالي المازج الحقيقي للمنطق الأرسطاطاليسي بعلوم المسلمين . لا لما وضع من كتب منطقية سهلة العبارة ، بل لتلك المقدمة المنطقية التي وضعها في أول كتابه المستصفى ، والتي ذكر فيها أن من لا يحيط بها فلا ثقة بعلومه قطعاً . وعلى هذا الأساس اعتبر منطق أرسطو شرطاً من شروط الاجتهاد وفرض كفاية على المسلمين ، ووجهت إلى الغزالي بسبب هذا اعتراضات شديدة من فقهاء المسلمين . ومنذ ذلك الحين بدأ الأصوليون المتكلمون يتأثرون بالمنطق الأرسططاليسي ويفردون في أول كتبهم فصلاً خاصاً لما أسموه « المقدمات الكلامية »(۲) أو « المقدمات الدخيلة » يلخصون فيها منطق أرسطو أو بمعنى أدق منطق الشراح الاسلاميين مشائياً تارة ورواقياً طوراً وكانت أكثر المباحث تأثراً بالمنطق اليوناني هذا ـ مباحث الألفاظ ـ أما مبحث القياس فقد استمر حتى بين أيدي الأصوليين المتأخرين بمنأى إلى أكبر حد عن هذا المنطق اليوناني أرسططاليسياً كان أو رواقياً . ولن نعرض في هذه الفصول لتلك المقدمات الكلامية . فقد سبق أن عرضنا لجميع أنواع المنطق اليوناني بين أيدي شراحه الإسلاميين . وتلك المقدمات ليست إلا صورة من هذه الشروح الجمة التي كتبها الإسلاميون والتي حللت عناصرها في الباب السابق . ولكن سنعرض لهذا المنهج الأصولي الكلامي - لأن المتكلمين يتشاركون فيه ، كما سنرى بعد ـ كما عرف قبل القرن الخامس . ولن أخوض في الأبحاث اللغوية لخروجها عن نطاق هذا البحث ، مع ملاحظة أن المباحث الأصولية اللغوية ليست من نوع علوم اللغة أو النحو العادية . فقد دقق الأصوليون نظرهم في فهم أشياء من كلام العرب لم يتوصل إليها اللغويون أو النحاة . إن كلام العرب متسع وطرق البحث فيه متشعبة . فكتب اللغة تضبط الألفاظ والمعاني الظاهرة دون المعاني الدقيقة التي يتوصل إليها الأصولي باستقراء يزيد على استقراء اللغوي . فهناك إذن دقائق لا يتعرض لها اللغوي ولا تقتضيها صناعة النحو . ولكن يتوصل إليها الأصوليون باستقراء خاص وأدلة خاصة(١) . هذا هو تاريخ المنهج الأصولي - Commentary
This passage is a historical overview of the relationship between Aristotelian logic and the Islamic science of usul al-fiqh. The author begins by mentioning Abu Hashim al-Jubbai, who attempted to mix logic with usul, and notes his departure from the method of the judge (likely al-Qadi 'Abd al-Jabbar) and his followers towards Mu'tazilite positions. He also denied God's knowledge of particulars, which placed him in opposition to the majority. The author then highlights al-Ghazali as the true mixer of Aristotelian logic with Islamic sciences, not merely through his simplified logical writings but because of the logical introduction he placed at the beginning of his work 'al-Mustasfa', where he declared that anyone who does not master logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge. This elevated Aristotelian logic to a condition for ijtihad and a collective obligation (fard kifaya). This provoked strong opposition from jurists. Subsequently, usuli theologians began to incorporate a chapter called 'theological introductions' (al-muqaddimat al-kalamiyya) or 'incoming introductions' in their works, summarizing Aristotle's logic as interpreted by Islamic commentators, sometimes Peripatetic, sometimes Stoic. The most affected area was the study of words (alfaz), while the study of analogy (qiyas) remained largely untouched by Greek logic. The author notes that he will not cover those theological introductions here, as he has already analyzed Greek logic in the hands of its Islamic commentators in a previous chapter. Instead, he will present the usuli-kalami methodology as it existed before the fifth Islamic century. He then addresses the distinct nature of linguistic usul researches, which go beyond ordinary language sciences and grammar; usulis have developed their own inductive methods to grasp subtle meanings not accessible to linguists. The passage concludes by summarizing the history: usul methodology was formed early and developed independently, was systematized by al-Shafi'i without Greek influence, split into fiqhi and kalami usul, still without Aristotelian influence until the fifth century when mixing occurred, which the author views as potentially stifling creative thinking. The passage ends by promising a discussion on the attitude of kalam theologians (usul al-din) towards Aristotelian logic in the next chapter.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which topic in usul al-fiqh was most influenced by Greek logic?
A) Qiyas (legal analogy)
B) Ijtihad
C) Mabahith al-alfaz (topics of words)
D) Ijma' (consensus)

Key Takeaway
The integration of Aristotelian logic into usul was partial: it affected the study of words but left legal analogy (qiyas) largely independent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine a usul text like al-Shirazi's al-Luma' and identify which sections show Aristotelian influence and which do not. Compare the treatment of al-alfaz with the treatment of qiyas.
?
Construct a simple qiyas (legal analogy) on a fiqh issue (e.g., the prohibition of nabidh by analogy to wine) and note how it differs from a categorical syllogism in terms of structure.

The Independent Origin and Later Mixing of Usul
Author summarizes the history of usul methodology and its independence before mixing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the timeline of usul al-fiqh's development showing its independence from Greek logic until the 5th century.

Core Idea
Usul methodology was formed independently by al-Shafi'i and remained free of Aristotelian logic until Ghazali.

The passage provides a sweeping historical summary: usul methodology was formed in the early Islamic period, continually refined, and then systematized by al-Shafi'i into a coherent science. Importantly, it was not influenced by Greek methods. After al-Shafi'i, usul split into fiqhi and kalami branches, and still remained unaffected by Aristotle's logic. Only in the 5th century (11th CE) did the mixing occur, and the author suggests this may have ended creative thinking in logic. This timeline challenges any notion that Islamic legal theory was derivative of Greek philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pre-mixing period
Find the phrases that describe usul before the 5th century: 'mundhu al-'asr al-awwal' (since the first era), 'hatta wasala ila yadi al-Shafi'i' (until it reached al-Shafi'i). Note the absence of Greek influence.
Al-Shafi'i is credited with establishing usul as a science with consistent parts.
2
Note the split after al-Shafi'i
The passage says usul split into 'ilm al-usul al-fiqhi' and 'ilm al-usul al-kalami'. Both remained unaffected by Aristotle's logic.
This shows that the theological and legal branches each developed independently.
3
Identify the turning point
The phrase 'hatta ata al-qarn al-khamis fa mazaja al-muslimun al-mantiq al-arsutalisi bil-usul' marks the 5th century as the time of mixing. The author adds a negative judgment: 'wa bihadha intaha aw kadu yantahi tafkir al-muslimin al-mubdi' fi al-mantiq' (with this ended, or almost ended, the creative thinking of Muslims in logic).
This is a critical perspective on the integration.
